### Post by elpichi on 2007-10-11
talking about gutsy release, is there a safe unformatting way to upgrade to this new version? =]

---

### Post by Frak on 2007-10-11
on the 18th your Update Manager will alert you to update your current Distribution (Feisty) to the newer (Gutsy)

---

### Post by misfitpierce on 2007-10-11
If you wait another week(7days) update manager will offer you option at top. If you want beta-RC and want to upgrade you type sudo apt-get dist-upgrade -c -d or something of the sort and it will open update manager with it at top. Note upgrading does take time depending on speed... at least 700MB worth of updates. :)

I would wait until 18th when it gives you the option auto when 7.10 is fully done.

---

### Post by misfitpierce on 2007-10-11
Yes if you keep up to date it will take you to final. I would say it is pretty safe to upgrade now. But there may be minor bugs in some things such as sleep or so on. I would recommend waiting 7 more days. Not that long to ensure a bug free environment with everything working. :)

### Post by Frak on 2007-10-16
Also, those who are running Gutsy Development, if you've updated to the latest and run
```
sudo lsb_release -a
```
You should come up with this
```
No LSB modules are available.
Distributor ID: Ubuntu
Description:    Ubuntu 7.10
Release:        7.10
Codename:       gutsy
```

No matter what your running, it'll just say Ubuntu (i.e. Kubuntu and Xubuntu come up as Ubuntu)

If you don't see "(Development Branch)" after Description: Ubuntu 7.10, then your running the final version of Gutsy :)

It would take a lot of heat off of the servers if people would go ahead and download it early and they apt-get upgrade when it "officially" releases. I'm certainly not trying to ruin the mood for anyone that loves the suspense, but for those of you who seem less concerned about that and more so about the bugfixes, it's a good idea to go ahead and download it now.

### Post by socceroos on 2007-10-17
Yeah, I can't wait for the release either. I've been using Ubuntu since tribe 5 and have really enjoyed the ride.

I must say it was a bit of a learning curve when trying to map a Windows 2003 Server shared printer.

Also, my laptop refuses to awaken from sleep. I have to kill the power.  AND, when pluggin in a projector to the VGA connector the screen flashes a few times and then Gutsy tells me it needs to run in Safe graphics mode. Nothing is displayed to the projector. APART from that, its GREAT.

I've noticed that the new printer options gives you the choice to 'Scale to fit' when you print a document! THIS IS A GREAT FEATURE!!!!

My boss soooo badly wanted this feature as all of our letterhead documents are PDF's with no margins.

Thanks Ubuntu Dev Team!!!!

### Post by RebounD11 on 2007-10-17
About that game we could play FAZAN ... it's a game we play in Romania to pass the time. It's something like this: a guy says a letter (actually it goes trough the alphabet another one sais when to stop). Then the one who said stop has to say a word starting with the letter at which the alphabet stopped. The next guy has to say a word that starts with the last to letters of the last word that was said and so on.

For example we have players 1,2,3 & 4.
1 recites the alphabet
2 sais stop
1 sais the letter he reached let's say R
2 sais for example Random
3 sais OMnipotent for example
since there is no word that starts with NT 4 is locked so he has an F and he has to say the alphabet and the cycle repeats.

Everytime a person is blocked he/she gets another letter. When U reach FAZAN U lose :D

Hope I've been pretty clear. Maybe we can adapt this game to the forum :D

### Post by BoyMike on 2007-10-17
The torrent files can be found [here]("http://www.ubuntu.com/getubuntu/downloadmirrors"). Not all locations have a torrent file availible, how ever most of them do, just pick the one you want, it might be called something like this "ubuntu-7.10-desktop-amd64.iso.torrent". Unless you have removed the BitTorrent client it should either be opened right away or saved somewhere and you'll have to open it your self.

### Post by cogadh on 2007-10-17
Does your ISP cap torrent downloads or something? If you have your torrent client configured correctly, you can max out your available bandwidth (I don't recommend that) and download Ubuntu in mere minutes without burdening the mirrors at all. Also, it doesn't matter how fast you upload, as long as you do upload. Since torrents are downloaded in chunks from multiple sources, your upload speed would only be one small piece of the total download picture.

---

### Post by southernman on 2007-10-17
> **kingofpain said:**
> Torrents are not necessarily a better solution than mirrors. From a mirror in my country I can download with 5MB/s, so it will take just a few minutes to transfer. With a torrent, I can dld maximum 250KB/s, and upload just a fraction of that...
It isn't being asked to use torrents, for a convience to you (or anyone) but to ease the burden on the servers, what's a couple of hours anyway (about what it would take a 250 KB/s). Not to mention that whatever speed you can upload at... a seed is a seed, is a seed.

It's about the bigger picture kop.

:rolleyes:

### Post by Trebaruna on 2007-10-17
[QUOTE=kingofpain]I was trying to say that I can dld in a few minutes, so the mirror is very fast available to someone else. I got the picture  ;) Maybe yo're right...[/QUOTE]

Just to note: even though you're using less time, the total bandwidth you use is still the same. So it's either longer time and less strain per time interval, or shorter time with a higher strain.
On the other hand, leeching is what those servers are there for, and nobody is forcing you to use torrents. :)
For me, I think I will, the speed should be good, and I'd like to help serve copies to others.

### Post by Rhapsody on 2007-10-17
I've now got my three-stage plan for Gutsy finalized.

1) Download the Kubuntu Gutsy Desktop CD (and seed it a bit), then burn it to a CD-R.
2) Attempt a straight upgrade from Feisty and see if it fixes anything. If so, stick with it. If not, try some further investigation, then proceed to step 3 if anything is still broken.
3) Peruse the home partition, delete or archive anything that looks like a configuration file, then delete root and start a clean install.

### Post by jamesford on 2007-10-17
just a little thing guys, if u install check4change [http://check4change.mozdev.org/](http://check4change.mozdev.org/) and open [http://releases.ubuntu.com/gutsy/](http://releases.ubuntu.com/gutsy/) and highlight the "The release candidate is no longer available..." text, rightclick and choose check4change u can have it check for u every x min/sec and display a notification when the page has changed, in the check4change preferences theres also an option to play a sound when this happens. this sound is located in ~/.mozilla/firefox/XXX.default/extensions/check4change-owner@mozdev.org/chrome/content/change.wav and can be replaced by any wav of your choice

so u can go to pick a loud sound, turn up the volume and go to bed and if ur pc isnt too far away from bed you can hear when gutsy hits the servers :)

---

### Post by jasay on 2007-10-17
> **pmoseley said:**
> 1) Anyone know what time band the ISO file servers are in?

2) Will upgrading to the RC now via 'update-manager -d' then upgrading any packages or whatever tomorrow land me with problems in the long run?

3) If I upgrade from Feisty to Gusty RC then to Gusty Final will Compiz Fusion still work 'out-of-the-box'?

PHIL BOI
1) There are mirrors all over the world, but Ubuntu is headquartered on the Isle of Man, so Greenwich Mean Time I believe.  Do note, however, that previous releases have not come at exactly the stroke of midnight.

2) Shouldn't.  I started with Gutsy 4 months ago and still going strong (I've actually been using this partition to upgrade from development version to development version since Breezy Badger).  There have only been a few updates since the RC anyway.

3) Assuming your video card is supported, then yes.

### Post by Chickenmonger on 2007-10-17
> **Method9455 said:**
> hmm no Kubuntu final release yet? I could just do the RC but I'd like to get on the main one so I can seed tomorrow when a bunch people crush the torrent. 

(Why doesn't the Ubuntu main page link more directly to torrent? It seemed like the primary link last time was a normal server I definitely didn't use torrent last time)

The Kubuntu release has an infohash of AAB5B0C88698D3422D2E24F9A4B166FACE581CE8. They're all named the same, but the comment within each torrent denotes the specific release. The Ubuntu release has an infohash of 30b96b535f4ae30f2dd9f1500a9110249c490a7a, by the way.

### Post by bigboy_pdb on 2007-10-18
I've seen a few people mention the timer being 00 but there's no release version of Ubuntu 7.10. The reason the timer says 00 is because the timer that counts down isn't based on the time of release. It's based on the day of release. If you look at the javascript for the timer, you'll see that it's based on your computer's clock and not on the time for one of their servers.

[http://www.ubuntu.com/files/countdown/dist/display.js](http://www.ubuntu.com/files/countdown/dist/display.js)

---

### Post by misfitpierce on 2007-10-18
> **conphara said:**
> Anybody's opinion on whether or not it's a good idea to use the 64 bit version of Gutsy. Will I have problems by using flash, java or other things?
What about the availability of 64 bit apps versus 32 bit, are there still a lot more in 32 bit.


May as well clear this up... Good question...

I am on 64 bit gutsy and upon opening firefox for first time on youtube etc you will notice a pop up. On Fesity this did nothing for 64 bit sadly... But on Gutsy it will auto download nspluginwrapper with adobe flash and install, restart firefox and it works. I recommend not using Gnash as it is still full of bugs... select Adobe. As for programs... Everything pretty much has a 64 bit component now that has a 32. If not you simply install using terminal like this to the 32 bit deb.
sudo dpkg --force-architecture -i NAME.deb
That will force install of 32 bit package on 64 bit OS. If it says it needs some stuff it may not auto grab where you hit up synaptic pack mngr and install what it needs. So I would recommend 64 bit highly. :)

---

### Post by misfitpierce on 2007-10-18
Theoretically 32 bit support the full 4GB, but your hardware is going to allocate some of the *address space *(not the physical RAM) to the PCI bus, the video adapter memory address space, and other resources. 32-bit OSs need to use part of the full 4GB address space to address these resources, subtracting from the maximum memory you have available to the OS and applications.

So under 4GB... The architecture on 64 can add tons of memory.  Exactly 17,179,869,184 gigabytes of ram. :)

### Post by misfitpierce on 2007-10-18
> **<<joe>> said:**
> i think the wiki is incorrect i will dobble check i think they just have a type-O 
need to change for Gigabyte to Gigabit


Very doubtful... Did you happen to read this part?

>    For example, the [x86]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/X86") architecture includes the [x87]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/X87") floating-point instructions which use 8 80-bit registers in a stack configuration; later revisions of x86, and the [x86-64]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/X86-64") architecture, also include [SSE]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Streaming_SIMD_Extensions") instructions, which use 8 128-bit wide registers (_**16 registers in x86-64**_). By contrast, the 64-bit [Alpha]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DEC_Alpha") family of processors defines 32 64-bit wide floating point registers in addition to its 32 64-bit wide integer registers.

Yeah. It's definitely done at the byte level. And the most common arrangement of bytes is by "words". For a 32 bit processor, a word is 4 bytes (32 bits). For a 64 bit processor, a word is techinically 8 bytes (64 bits).

### Post by remitaylor on 2007-10-18
> **<<joe>> said:**
> post the script

i would like to uses

and in an  open source community its only right
script: 

--> [http://pastie.caboo.se/108400](http://pastie.caboo.se/108400) <--

it's its own web app, so it'd be easy to customize (or simply because i was bored) ... I'm sure I could've used an iframe instead, but I wanted to include the last N posts, regardless of how many posts are on the current page.

Simply grabs the current page of posts (+ the previous if there are less than 10 posts on the current page) and spits out the author, posted time, and content.  pulls the ubuntuforums stylesheet to make it look about the same, but some of the emoticons don't show up.

All in ~ 100 lines

Let all know ... *this* is how bored we get waiting for Gutsy to friggin greet the masses, already!

### Post by Chadwill on 2007-10-18
[COLOR="Red"][SIZE="6"]DO NOT DOWNLOAD YET!![/SIZE][/COLOR]

from IRC:

(11:55:37) tonyyarusso: Okay, I just wanted to take a second to explain what the deal with links and mirrors and such is.

(11:56:12) tonyyarusso: I was just talking to some of the folks from the release team, and the way things work they start

(11:56:37) tonyyarusso: That way they get the most bandwidth-intensive part done overnight.  After that, rsync does just incremental changes to the files.

(11:56:57) tonyyarusso: So, the files are up, and about the right size for an ISO, but still not the final product.

(11:57:59) tonyyarusso: Meanwhile, having people download those does 2 things: 1) hammers bandwidth that's needed for rsyncing the changes so it CAN be final, and 2) users may end up with something that's not really the right, final product without knowing it.

(11:58:07) tonyyarusso: Hope that clears it up a bit

### Post by PartisanEntity on 2007-10-18
Posting this from another thread:

> **Chadwill said:**
> [COLOR=Red][SIZE=6]DO NOT DOWNLOAD YET!![/SIZE][/COLOR]

from IRC:

(11:55:37) tonyyarusso: Okay, I just wanted to take a second to explain what the deal with links and mirrors and such is.

(11:56:12) tonyyarusso: I was just talking to some of the folks from the release team, and the way things work they start

(11:56:37) tonyyarusso: That way they get the most bandwidth-intensive part done overnight.  After that, rsync does just incremental changes to the files.

(11:56:57) tonyyarusso: So, the files are up, and about the right size for an ISO, but still not the final product.

(11:57:59) tonyyarusso: Meanwhile, having people download those does 2 things: 1) hammers bandwidth that's needed for rsyncing the changes so it CAN be final, and 2) users may end up with something that's not really the right, final product without knowing it.

(11:58:07) tonyyarusso: Hope that clears it up a bit

For those who want to download it, please wait until it is officially released on ubuntu.com

(11:55:37) tonyyarusso: Okay, I just wanted to take a second to explain what the deal with links and mirrors and such is.

(11:56:12) tonyyarusso: I was just talking to some of the folks from the release team, and the way things work they start

(11:56:37) tonyyarusso: That way they get the most bandwidth-intensive part done overnight.  After that, rsync does just incremental changes to the files.

(11:56:57) tonyyarusso: So, the files are up, and about the right size for an ISO, but still not the final product.

(11:57:59) tonyyarusso: Meanwhile, having people download those does 2 things: 1) hammers bandwidth that's needed for rsyncing the changes so it CAN be final, and 2) users may end up with something that's not really the right, final product without knowing it.

### Post by damianvila on 2007-10-18
I believe the guys at IRC are talking about web download, since all the HTTP stuff is pretty much inneficient, compared to torrent. You need to mirror the web page and ALL the files (wich may take some time.)
The torrents, I believe, are OK. If they pass the checksum, then they are it (and after all, it doesn't hurt to download from torrent).
If you're unsure about your torrent just wait till they make the HTTP download official and do a new checksum. The wors scenario would be that you'll have to redownload the ISO.
If you are sure or you don't mind, just install it and anjoy it (it will be a pretty stable RC, after all).
But saying that the ISOs are fake, is pretty silly... :p
Just don't use the web download until the full deployment has taken place, so everybody will be benefited.

#define TYPEbinary  1
#define ARCH  i386
#define ARCHi386  1
#define DISKNUM  1
#define DISKNUM1  1
#define TOTALNUM  0
#define TOTALNUM0  1

### Post by damianvila on 2007-10-18
> **potentia said:**
> 1) I hope upgrading works here, it did with Feisty.
2) Not really, I just use it (install quite a lot, but no problems). I hear the argument quite often, and it makes me smile. I heard the argument so often from Linux enthusiasts that they ran away from the many reinstalls of Windows, and then they do the same with Linux (for different reasons, but still). Reinstall. I hate reinstalling, I want to use my computer, not play with it, so this easy upgrade just have to work for me.

Let's see how this upgrade ends. :)

When I upgraded to Feisty, I followed a tutorial to enable Beryl on my machine. When Beryl/Compiz was made a part of the system, I losed 3D acceleration and the effects, and was unable to get it back. I upgraded last night with the hope that the problem will be solved... to no avail.
So, in my case, even after an upgrade, I need a fresh install.
You must keep in mind that there's still problem with some graphic card drivers (that thankfully will be solved very soon), so if you ruined something in your config and don't know how to solve it (like in my case) you'll drag the problem to the new system when you upgrade, since upgrading respects your (flawed) config.

### Post by greg.hagen on 2007-10-18
For everyone who is trying to figure out if their torrent dl from like 8 hours ago is the right one:

md5sum ./ubuntu-7.10-desktop-amd64.iso 
61c87943a92bc7bf519da4e2555d6e86  ./ubuntu-7.10-desktop-amd64.iso

From the website:
61c87943a92bc7bf519da4e2555d6e86 *ubuntu-7.10-desktop-amd64.iso

Those torrents are the correct version!

Gutsy is awesome. Incredibly stable, even with Compiz-fusion, apache2, mysql-server, proftpd, and openssh-server all running at the same time. Seeding whenever im going to be off the computer for half an hour or more, 800mb last night, another 350 earlier today. Demand is certainly slowing down :D

Cant get over the boot time. 20second reduction and actually being able to run in a resolution higher than 1024x768. Now my head doesnt explode every time i hit my KVM switch after being on my 1280x1024 Windows box.

---
